<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">WWE Hall of Fame</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em">
<caption class="fn org">WWE Hall of Fame</caption>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WWEHallofFameRender.png"><img alt="WWEHallofFameRender.png" data-file-height="183" data-file-width="280" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/93/WWEHallofFameRender.png/250px-WWEHallofFameRender.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/9/93/WWEHallofFameRender.png 1.5x" width="250"/></a>
<div>WWE Hall of Fame logo, used since 2015</div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>

</tr>
<tr>

9 celebrities<br/>

(147 total inductees)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>WWE Hall of Fame</b> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hall_of_fame" title="Hall of fame">hall of fame</a> for <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling" title="Professional wrestling">professional wrestling</a> personalities maintained by <a href="/wiki/WWE" title="WWE">WWE</a>. It was announced on the March 22, 1993 episode of <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_Raw" title="WWE Raw">Monday Night Raw</a></i> where <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_the_Giant" title="André the Giant">André the Giant</a>, who had died nearly two months prior, was announced as the sole inductee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWFRawMar22_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-WWFRawMar22-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Andre_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Andre-3">[3]</a></sup> The 1994 and 1995 ceremonies were held in conjunction with the annual <a href="/wiki/King_of_the_Ring" title="King of the Ring">King of the Ring</a> pay-per-view events. In 1996, the ceremony was held with the <a href="/wiki/Survivor_Series" title="Survivor Series">Survivor Series</a> event, for the first time in front of a paying audience as well as the wrestlers, after which, the Hall of Fame went on hiatus.</p>
<p>In 2004, WWE relaunched the Hall of Fame to coincide with <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_XX" title="WrestleMania XX">WrestleMania XX</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2004h_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-2004h-4">[4]</a></sup> This ceremony, like its predecessors, was not broadcast on television. However, it was released on <a href="/wiki/DVD" title="DVD">DVD</a> on June 1, 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Beginning with the 2005 ceremony, an edited version of the Hall of Fame was broadcast on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spike_(TV_channel)" title="Spike (TV channel)">Spike TV</a> (2005)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2005h_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-2005h-6">[6]</a></sup> and on the <a href="/wiki/USA_Network" title="USA Network">USA Network</a> (2006<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup>–present<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wrestleview1_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wrestleview1-8">[8]</a></sup>); these were aired on <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_delay" title="Broadcast delay">tape delay</a>. Since 2005, the entire Hall of Fame ceremony has been packaged as part of the annual WrestleMania DVD release,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> and from 2014, has been broadcast live on the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Network" title="WWE Network">WWE Network</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> In 2015, historical WWE Hall of Fame ceremonies became available on the WWE Network.</p>
<p>Although a building has never been built to represent the Hall of Fame, WWE has looked into constructing a facility. In 2008, <a href="/wiki/Shane_McMahon" title="Shane McMahon">Shane McMahon</a>, then-Executive Vice President of Global Media of WWE, stated that WWE had been storing wrestling memorabilia in a warehouse for years, with all items categorized and dated in case a facility is created.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Facility_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Facility-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2016, there have been 147 inductees – with 100 wrestlers inducted individually, 10 group inductions (consisting of 29 wrestlers within those groups), nine celebrities, two Warrior Award recipients, and seven Legacy Inductees. 35 members were inducted posthumously. <a href="/wiki/Ric_Flair" title="Ric Flair">Ric Flair</a> is the only Hall of Famer to be inducted twice, first individually in 2008, then as a member of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Four_Horsemen_(professional_wrestling)" title="Four Horsemen (professional wrestling)">The Four Horsemen</a> in 2012, while Flair and <a href="/wiki/Sting_(wrestler)" title="Sting (wrestler)">Sting</a> are the only people to be inducted while still active.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HoF_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-HoF-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HoF_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-HoF-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

His association with <a href="/wiki/Cyndi_Lauper" title="Cyndi Lauper">Cyndi Lauper</a> was pivotal in turning professional wrestling into a mainstream phenomenon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Albano_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Albano-30">[30]</a></sup></td>

<i>As of September 2015, Jimmy Snuka's profile is no longer in the Hall of Fame section at WWE.com. However, this does not necessarily mean that Snuka has been removed from the WWE Hall of Fame completely. No statement has been made by WWE yet about this matter, however his name remained on the list of inductees for that year in the third volume of the</i> WWE Encyclopedia <i>released in 2016.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>

<td rowspan="2">2009</td>
<td><b><a href="/wiki/Von_Erich_family" title="Von Erich family">The Von Erichs</a></b></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Michael_Hayes_(wrestler)" title="Michael Hayes (wrestler)">Michael Hayes</a></td>
<td><small>Noted wrestling family that spent many years wrestling in <a href="/wiki/World_Class_Championship_Wrestling" title="World Class Championship Wrestling">World Class Championship Wrestling</a> (WCCW). Various combinations of the family held several NWA regional and WCCW tag team championships, including the <a href="/wiki/WCWA_World_Tag_Team_Championship" title="WCWA World Tag Team Championship">WCCW World Tag Team</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WCCW_World_Six-Man_Tag_Team_Championship" title="WCCW World Six-Man Tag Team Championship">World Six-Man Tag Team Championship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></small></td>

<tr>
<td colspan="3"><a href="/wiki/Fritz_Von_Erich" title="Fritz Von Erich">Fritz Von Erich</a> (Jack Adkisson) – Posthumous inductee: Founder and longtime owner of WCCW, one-time <a href="/wiki/AWA_World_Heavyweight_Championship" title="AWA World Heavyweight Championship">AWA World Heavyweight Champion</a> and 16-time <a href="/wiki/WCWA_World_Heavyweight_Championship" title="WCWA World Heavyweight Championship">NWA American Heavyweight Champion</a> (later renamed the WCCW World Heavyweight Championship).<br/>
<a href="/wiki/Kevin_Von_Erich" title="Kevin Von Erich">Kevin Von Erich</a> (Kevin Adkisson) – Six-time NWA American/WCCW World Heavyweight Champion.<br/>
<a href="/wiki/David_Von_Erich" title="David Von Erich">David Von Erich</a> (David Adkisson) – Posthumous inductee: Eight-time <a href="/wiki/WCWA_World_Heavyweight_Championship" title="WCWA World Heavyweight Championship">NWA Texas Heavyweight Champion</a>.<br/>
<a href="/wiki/Kerry_Von_Erich" title="Kerry Von Erich">Kerry Von Erich</a> (Kerry Adkisson) – Posthumous inductee: One-time NWA World Heavyweight Champion, nine-time NWA American/WCCW World Heavyweight Champion. Wrestled in WWF as "The Texas Tornado" where he was a one-time <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WWF_Intercontinental_Champion" title="WWF Intercontinental Champion">WWF Intercontinental Champion</a>.<br/>
<a href="/wiki/Mike_Von_Erich" title="Mike Von Erich">Mike Von Erich</a> (Michael Adkisson) – Posthumous inductee: One-time NWA American Heavyweight Champion.<br/>
<a href="/wiki/Chris_Von_Erich" title="Chris Von Erich">Chris Von Erich</a> (Chris Adkisson) – Posthumous inductee: Wrestled and worked several backstage jobs for WCCW.</td>

<a href="/wiki/Road_Warrior_Animal" title="Road Warrior Animal">Road Warrior Animal</a> (Joseph Laurinaitis) – One-time <a href="/wiki/WWE_Raw_Tag_Team_Championship" title="WWE Raw Tag Team Championship">WWE Tag Team Champion</a> (without Hawk)<br/>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Warrior_Award">Warrior Award</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dana_Warrior_Award.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2693" data-file-width="1515" height="302" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Dana_Warrior_Award.jpg/170px-Dana_Warrior_Award.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Dana_Warrior_Award.jpg/255px-Dana_Warrior_Award.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Dana_Warrior_Award.jpg/340px-Dana_Warrior_Award.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dana_Warrior_Award.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dana Warrior presents the inaugural Warrior Award at the 2015 Hall of Fame ceremony</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2015, WWE introduced the Warrior Award for those who have "exhibited unwavering strength and perseverance, and who lives life with the courage and compassion that embodies the indomitable spirit of the Ultimate Warrior."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Connor_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-Connor-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>While WWE promotes Warrior Award recipients as Hall of Fame inductees,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> they are not included in the Hall of Fame section at WWE.com.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> and an image gallery which shows "every WWE Hall of Famer ever" does not contain either recipient.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>The award was created following <a href="/wiki/The_Ultimate_Warrior" title="The Ultimate Warrior">The Ultimate Warrior</a>'s death. During his April 2014 Hall of Fame speech shortly before his death, he proposed that there be a special category called the "Jimmy Miranda Award" for WWE's behind-the-scenes employees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> Miranda, who died in 2002, was part of the WWE merchandise department for more than 20 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> Former WWE ring announcer <a href="/wiki/Justin_Roberts" title="Justin Roberts">Justin Roberts</a> expressed disappointment at how WWE used portions of Warrior's Hall of Fame speech to promote the award, but left out Warrior's intentions of honoring WWE's off-screen employees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RobertsTorch_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-RobertsTorch-148">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RobertsInsider_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-RobertsInsider-149">[149]</a></sup> WWE responded, "It is offensive to suggest that WWE and its executives had anything but altruistic intentions in honoring <a href="/wiki/Connor_Michalek" title="Connor Michalek">Connor</a> and his legacy with The Warrior Award", adding that "moving forward the award will be given annually to acknowledge other unsung heroes among WWE's employees and fans."</p>
<p>Traditionally, Dana Warrior (widow of The Ultimate Warrior) will present the award.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy_inductees">Legacy inductees</span></h3>
<p>In 2016, WWE introduced a new category for the Hall of Fame called the "Legacy" wing. Inductees under this new category feature wrestlers from the early years of professional wrestling, primarily during the early part of the 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Legacy_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-Legacy-151">[151]</a></sup> All inductees thus far have been inducted posthumously and were recognized with a video package at the ceremony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bruno_Sammartino" title="Bruno Sammartino">Bruno Sammartino</a>, the longest reigning <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WWE_World_Heavyweight_Champion" title="WWE World Heavyweight Champion">WWWF World Heavyweight Champion</a>, was once critical of the Hall of Fame. Sammartino disapproved of celebrity inductees such as <a href="/wiki/Pete_Rose" title="Pete Rose">Pete Rose</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Perry_(American_football)" title="William Perry (American football)">William Perry</a>, and said of the ceremony: "What's the point to a Hall of Fame? Is it a building I can actually go to? No. Give me a break".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Slam2_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-Slam2-167">[167]</a></sup> Sammartino declined induction several times, before accepting in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> Sammartino later claimed that "Being inducted into the Hall of Fame at <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a> is the biggest thing in my life".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Hall has garnered criticism due to the inductions of questionable performers, and the omissions of major names within the industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bob_Backlund" title="Bob Backlund">Bob Backlund</a> declined induction multiple times,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eck_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-eck-172">[172]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/The_Ultimate_Warrior" title="The Ultimate Warrior">The Ultimate Warrior</a> wrote that he refused the honor in 2010;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> they were eventually inducted in 2013 and 2014, respectively. <a href="/wiki/Randy_Savage" title="Randy Savage">Randy Savage</a> was recognized as being noticeably absent;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chris_Jericho" title="Chris Jericho">Chris Jericho</a> said that the Hall achieved a level of legitimacy by inducting him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Superstar_Billy_Graham" title="Superstar Billy Graham">Superstar Billy Graham</a> publicly slammed the hall and demanded that WWE remove him from it, due to the 2011 induction of <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_the_Butcher" title="Abdullah the Butcher">Abdullah the Butcher</a>. Graham wrote: "It is a shameless organization to induct a bloodthirsty animal such as Abdullah the Butcher into their worthless and embarrassing Hall of Fame and I want the name of Superstar Billy Graham to be no part of it".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup></p>
<p>2015 Hall of Fame headliner <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Nash" title="Kevin Nash">Kevin Nash</a> stated that two things in the professional wrestling business are real: "When you win your first championship and when you get inducted into the Hall of Fame." Nash claimed this is a sentiment to which colleague <a href="/wiki/Ric_Flair" title="Ric Flair">Ric Flair</a> also subscribes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup></p>
<p>Dave Scherer of <i>PWInsider</i> has questioned how WWE can sustain the 2004–present Hall of Fame model, due to legends being rapidly inducted. He wrote: "There are only so many people that they can have headline a class. They really need to make more new stars to ensure that they can keep filling arenas for the ceremony".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup></p>
